As only closed carapaces were available for study this species is provisionally placed in Semicytherura on the basis of the curved dorsal margin rather than in Cytherura where the type species is very different and has a straight dorsal margin. Nevertheless, when good material showing the internal features on which the generic differences are essentially drawn become available, it may be necessary to transfer this species to another genus of the Cytheruridae. The closest comparable species appears to be that from the lower Palaeocene of Saudi Arabia recorded as Semicytherura sp. by AI-Furaih (1980). The material figured here is closest to his presumed female dimorph in shape although not generally so vaulted dorsally nor so convex ventrally. The surface ornamentation is not well preserved in AI-Furaih's specimens but fine reticulation and ribbing were present and although the details cannot be made out the general size of the reticules is closely comparable with the Assam species. 781						Cytheridae	Cytherinae		Buntonia		Buntonia delta	Marianos and Valentine, 1958		Plate 1, figures 6a-b, 7		"Carapace medium-sized, pyriform; widest at posterior one-third line, highest at anterior cardinal angle. Dorsal margin nearly straight, slightly concave posteriorly; anterior margin broadly rounded above, more sharply rounded below; ventral margin gently convex, indented anterior to center; posterior margin narrow, narrowly rounded below and angled above; in left valve the posterior cardinal angle is somewhat produced. Surface ornamented by numerous low ridges, strongest on inflated posteroventral portion of valve, where they run in general longitudinally; dorsally and anteriorly they become nearly obsolete; interspaces between longitudinal ridges crossed by low, rather regularly spaced transverse ridges, which divide them into pits. Margin reflected posteroventrally to form a sinus, leaving a gape when valves are articulated; margin denticulate at sinus.
Hinge of right valve with rounded anterior tooth and subjacent socket, connected by a narrow groove to a longitudinally elongate posterior tooth. Hinge of left valve with anterior socket and rounded subjacent tooth, connected by narrow margin to longitudinally elongate posterior socket. Radial pore canals straight and numerous."		This species resembles Buntonia shubutaensis Howe var. morsei (Howe and Pyeatt), as described by Howe and Chambers (1935), but it is more coarsely pitted and is narrower and more acutely angulate posteriorly. It is dimorphic; the relatively short and broad form is figured. Dorsal margin straight or gently convex; anterior margin broadly rounded; ventral margin gently convex, indented just anterior to center; posterior margin angulated near center, convex both above and below angulation; dorsal and ventral margins converge posteriorly. Surface reticulate, with two low longitudinal ridges, one just above the center, the other ventral. Eye tubercle small. Margin raised, slightly reflected postero-ventrally to form a narrow sinus.
Hinge of right valve with rounded anterior tooth and postjacent socket connected by a narrow groove to a small, oval posterior tooth. Hinge of left valve with anterior socket and rounded postjacent tooth, connected by a narrow margin to an oval posterior socket. Radial pore canals narrow, numerous, commonly bifurcating; most numerous anteriorly."		Buntonia seco somewhat resembles Buntonia alabamensis (Howe and Pyeatt), as described by Howe and Garrett (1934), but it has more prominent longitudinal ridges and a wider but more acutely angulated posterior. It differs from Buntonia subtriangularis (Sutton and Williams) (1939) in having more subdued sculpture and a more evenly rounded anterior margin. Very rare at Fig-Tree Gulch.		0.50*0.14*0.36(Valve)	Marysville Buttes, California, USA	Fig-Tree Gulch				Capay		Eocene 					marine	gray-green, massive, glauconitic claystone. 784							Cytherurinae		Paijenborchella 		Paijenborchella trigona	Marianos and Valentine, 1958		Plate 2, figures 3a-b, 4, 5a-b		"Carapace small, thick, trigonal, markedly inflated, highest at anterior cardinal angle, widest slightly posterior to center. Dorsal margin of left valve broadly rounded, that of right valve straight and slightly inclined, dipping posteriorly; anterior margin broadly rounded; ventral margin strongly convex, indented anterior to center; posterior triangular, with caudal process along center line. Surface ornamented by deep median sulcus, longitudinal ridges, and pits; sulcus extends ventrally from anterior cardinal angle, terminating against a prominent ventral longitudinal ridge; between this ridge and ventral margin are two shorter, weaker ridges; a prominent ridge bridges the sulcus near center line; less prominent ridges extend both anteriorly and posteriorly from small eye tubercle parallel with dorsal margin; remainder of surface coarsely and evenly pitted. A broad accommodation groove (""Ausweichfurche"" of Kingma) lies between left hingement and dorsal margin."		Paijenborchella, which is reported from the late Cretaceous (Triebel, 1949) to the Recent (Ruggieri, 1953), has not previously been recorded from North America. Paijenborchella trigona is similar in shape to Paijenborchella eocenica (Triebel, 1949), but is thinner-shelled, has a shorter caudal process, and has a less prominent median ridge that lacks the hook-like projection. It is markedly dimorphic; the short form is figured. Very abundant at Fig-Tree Gulch.		0.57*0.31*0.29(Carapase)	Marysville Buttes, California, USA	Fig-Tree Gulch				Capay		Eocene 					marine	gray-green, massive, glauconitic claystone. 785						Trachyleberidae	Trachyleberinae		Trachyleberis 		Trachyleberis semihispida	Marianos and Valentine, 1958		Plate 1, figures 4a-b, 5		"Carapace medium-sized, thick, robust, elongate in side view; highest anteriorly, widest at posterior quarter-line. This species lacks the dorsal ridge and spiny, thickened posteroventral margin of Trachyleberis orelliana (Stadnichenko), which is well figured by Stephenson (1946). Trachyleberis semihispida is markedly dimorphic. The long form bears more prominent antero- and posteroventral denticulations, and has a large postero-ventral tubercle on the left valve. Individuals of either form may appear quite hispid if many large nodes are developed at the intersections of the reticulate ridges. The relatively short, broad form is figured. PI. 93, figs. 7			A species of Cytherelloidea characterized by two median rims; in females the ventral rim is essentially straight; the dorsal rim is curved down and around a depression which develops just above the center of the valve, and it dies out before it reaches the anterior or dorsum. Male valves are distinguished by the two median ribs which fail to connect to either anterior or posterior margins, dying out about equidistant from either end.	"This species shows marked sexual dimorphism. In female carapaces the posterodorsal and posteroventral portions of the valves are swollen, forming two circular pits on the inside and two raised nodes on the exterior. Male valves are much shallower, and lack the two circular posterior pits. The hinge is a modification of the peripheral lock, consisting of an upraised portion of the hingement in the left valve just behind the central depressed area which forms a raised flange that fits into a corresponding depression in the right valve.
In Howe & Chambers (1935), mention is made of the male of this species under the description of C. danvillensis (p. 7), wherein it is stated that a variety of C. danvillensis, differing from C. danvillensis ""in not having a low rounded semicircular ridge above the pit"" is common in nearly all marine lower Jackson localities. This variety is actually the male of C. montgomeryensis. The description in Howe & Chambers (1935) is that of a left valve of a female. The right valve of the female differs slightly, being larger and lacking the depressed area anterior to the center of the dorsal margin.
Muscle scars are located slightly above the middle of the carapace on a raised area which corresponds with the external depression. They consist of two closely adjacent rows arranged vertically; the front row consisting of seven scars, the top four long, thin, and longitudinally elongate, the third from the bottom much shorter, the bottom two very tiny and situated slightly posterior to the other five. The back row consists of eight scars, the top two similar to the ones in the front row. Two smaller scars lie immediately below this; subjacent to theseis another elongate scar, which is bounded ventrally by two smaller scars. A single elongate scar sits astride the top of the two rows."		"0.58*NA*0.34(LV)(F);

The name Budaia was applied to a lower Cretaceous trochosmiliid coral by Wells in 1933; therefore the name Budaia as applied by Mehes in 1941 to this genus is invalid. 810									Triginglymus		Triginglymus heistensis	Krutak, 1962		PI. 93, figs. 4,8,11		"Carapace in side view elongate, plump, length being about twice height. Dorsal and ventral margins parallel; both ends rounded, the anterior obliquely.
Surface of carapace pitted. A low rounded rim, paralleling the anterior, develops just inside the anterior outline. A smooth, transparent ""lucid"" spot near the center of the carapace marks the position of the muscle node. 
Viewed from the inside, the valves are rather deep, the interior divided by a low ridge behind the muscle pit. Marginal areas regular, widest anteriorly. Threadlike radial pore canals are numerous anteriorly, less so posteriorly.
Hingement holamphidont, modified in both valves by ""anti-slip"" teeth. A lobelike, longitudinally elongate projection (anti-slip tooth) develops just below the dorsal groove and behind the anterior socket in the right valve, and below the dorsal ridge and behind the anterior tooth in the left, being more depressed in this valve.
Muscle scars, located on the posterior border of a shallow pit which lies somewhat above and anterior to the middle of the carapace, consist of a vertical row of four adductors in front of which is a curved antennal scar, anteroventral to which are two mandibular scars."	A triginglymid species characterized in lateral outline by its produced anteroventral end, low rounded anterior rim, and longitudinally pitted surface.	"This species differs from T. hyperochus Blake of the Claiborne Gosport Sand in several ways: in its lateral outline, being less high and more produced antero-ventrally; in its almost truncate posterior end; being less swollen posteroventrally; having a low rim paralleling the anterior end; and in its surface ornamentation, which consists of pits instead of reticulations. Females are much more tumid posteriorly, and generally higher than the males although
relative length stays about the same. The new species is based on eighty-four single valves and fourteen whole carapaces. The specific name is derived from the Greek cave, pit, or hollow, and bearer, carrier."		"0.47*NA*0.23(RV)(M);

812							Hemicytherinae		Absonocytheropteron		Absonocytheropteron watervalleyensis	Krutak, 1962	 	Pl. 92, fig. 11		"Carapace in lateral view ovate-elongate; highest at anterior cardinal angle, longest just below the midline, thickest posteroventrally; arrowhead-like in dorsal view. Dorsal outline straight along hingeline, swelling up and around a slightly elevated eyespot at the anterior cardinal angle, converging rather strongly toward the posterior. Ventral margin obscured by the ventral swelling of the valve. Anterior end obliquely rounded, posterior end more narrowly rounded. Left valve overlaps right slightly at the anterior cardinal angle. Ventral side of valves almost flat, bearing longitudinal striations. Exterior of carapace essentially smooth except ventrally where a series of irregular depressions occurs. These are bordered by a shallow longitudinal furrow which parallels the ventral ala.
Viewed from the inside, the valves are rather deep; marginal areas are well developed; a weak vestibule is present anteriorly. Radial pore canals are numerous; approximately seven can be seen posteriorly and posteroventrally; numerous canals exist around the anterior marginal area.
Hingement holamphidont. Muscle scars consist of four adductor scars in a vertical row, in front of which are apparently two obliquely inclined antennal scars."	This species is recognized by its faintly sculptured carapace, weak alae, and lack of a subcentral tubercle.	The species shows strong sexual dimorphism, males being much longer and less plump. This species is based on twelve single valves and thirteen whole carapaces. The type species A. carinata Puri from the Crystal River Formation of Florida is set apart by its highly ornamented carapace, prominent subcentral tubercle, and more prominent alae. This species has been compared with Ocala species of the type species and on the basis of muscle scars may be questionably placed in the Hemicytherinae.		0.82*0.42*0.42(Carapase)(M)	Choctaw County, Alabama, USA	No.1/4/5			Jackson	Yazoo	Cocoa sand	Eocene 					shallow water (based on the ecology of ostracoda fossils)	sandstone		Krutak_1961_Jackson Eocene Ostracoda from the Cocoa Sand of Alabama.pdf

The species described above resembles the type species, Cushmanidea seminuda (Cushman, 1906), in general appearance and type of hinge, but differs in the details of the outline. Another species close to the present one is Cushmanidea sagena Benson and Kaesler, 1963, but in this species the ventral margin in the left valve is concave, whereas in the present species it is slightly convex. Cushmanidea panciradialis Swain and Gilby, 1967, a Recent species, also resembles the present species in appearance but differs in the length/height ratio. 835									Parakrithe		Parakrithe Pandei	Khosla, 1972		Plate 2, figures 24-25	Fuller's Earth beds of the Assilina granulosa Zone, Khuiala Formation (Lower Eocene), section 11.	Carapace elongate in lateral view, with maximum height posterior to middle; left valve slightly larger than right, with a distinct overlap at ventral and posterior margins; dorsal margin convex for most of its length, but slightly concave in anterodorsal part; ventral margin concave in anteroventral part and straight for rest of length; anterior margin broadly rounded; posterior margin downwardly rounded. In dorsal view, carapace compressed anteriorly; maximum width posterior to middle. Valve surface smooth.	This species shows some variation in the degree of concavity of the anterodorsal margin. It resembles the type species Parakrithe vermunti (van den Bold, 1946), described from the Lower Oligocene beds of Trinidad, in over-all shape and in the concavity at the anteroventral margin, but the latter species has comparatively more height and thus differs in length/height ratio. The present species in general appearance resembles also Parakrithe elongata van den Bold, 1960, described from the Middle Eocene and Lower Oligocene beds of Trinidad, but the latter species, unlike the present one, has a straight dorsal margin.			0.46*0.15*0.18(Carapase)	Rajasthan, India	sample P/B 10. 11 and 13 from section II	Section I (27.86; 72.93); Section II and III (27.83; 73.25); Section IV (27.18; 70.37)					Eocene								Khosla_1972_Ostracodes from the Eocene Beds of Rajasthan, India	In this paper, the description of new species is put under 'diagosis', and the diagnosis is put under 'discussion' column;

Plate 1, figure 15; plate 4, figure 2				Remarks: The species recorded herein was described as Schuleridea bhupendri (generic name misspelled as Shulredia) by Singh and Misra (supra cit.) from the Fuller's Earth beds of Mudh. According to van Morkhoven (1963), the genus Schuleridea is characterized by a very pronounced overlap, the hinge inthe right valve consisting of all projecting elements and that in the left valve all negative elements, and by numerous, closely spaced, marginal pore canals. As against this pattern, the present species has a different hinge (in the right valve consisting of anterior and posterior crenulated teeth connected by a groove, and complementary elements in the left valve), a slignt overlap, and a few straight, marginal pore canals. On the basis of these characters, the species is transferred to the genus Neocyprideis.		"0.70*0.36*0.45(Carapase)(F);

Plate 2, figure 4; plate 4, figure 4				Remarks: This species has been previously described from the Eocene beds of Kutch as Trachyleberis memorans by Lubimova and Guha (supra cit.). However, it has surface ornamentation and hinge structure unlike those of the genus Trachyleberis. The surface of each valve is coarsely reticulate and has a dorsal ridge slightly protruding above the margin, a ventral ridge sloping upwards posteriorly, a prominent subcentral tubercle, and a crescent-shaped depression posterior to it. The hinge is of amphidont/heterodont type. In the right valve it consists of a pointed anterior tooth, a post-jacent socket which continues into a long groove, and a large, smooth, posterior tooth. The hinge in the left valve is complementary. On the basis of these characters the species is transferred to the genus Anticythereis. Singh and Misra (supra cit.) created three new species: Quadracythere gautami, Trachyleberis deshpandi, and T. mathuri. These appear to be conspecific and are here questionably considered as junior synonyms of A. memorans. Quadracythere? aspinosa Sohn, 1970, described from the Meting Limestone of Pakistan, is definitely a junior synonym of A. memorans.		0.83*0.26*0.46(RV)(F)	Rajasthan, India	"Venericardia mutabilis Zone of section I;

844									Buntonia 		Buntonia boldi			Plate 2, figures 13-14; plate 5, figure 3	Grey shales of the Assilina granulosa Zone, Khuiala Formation (Lower Eocene), section III.	Carapace oval in lateral view, with maximum height anterior to middle; left valve slightly overlapping right valve; dorsal margin weakly arched; ventral margin convex; anterior end broadly rounded; posterior end less so. Carapace biconvex in dorsal view; maximum width posterior to middle. Surface of each valve covered with closely spaced pits. A vertical sulcus extends from the central dorsal margin downwards to two-thirds of the height, a short but distinct ridge traversing the sulcus near the centre. Sexual dimorphism distinct; male carapace more elongate than female carapace.	The internal features of the species are not well preserved. According to Dr. H. V. Howe, to whom the present specimens from Rajasthan were sent, the external characters are quite distinctive enough for the species to be assigned to the genus Buntonia. The species resembles Buntonia shubutaensis Howe, 1935 (in Howe and Chambers, 1935), the type species described from the Upper Eocene Jackson beds, in over-all shape and in some other characters. The present species differs distinctly, however, from B. shubutaensis and many other species of the genus Buntonia in the presence of a vertical sulcus, traversed by a short ridge near the centre. In B. shubutaensis the surface is ornamented by ridges and furrows in the posterior half. Buntonia (Protobuntonia) punctata Reyment, 1963, a Paleocene species, somewhat resembles the present species in general shape and surface ornamentation, but differs in the absence of a vertical sulcus and in minor details of the outline. 855									Ruggieria		Ruggieria bhatiai	Khosla, 1972		Plate 3, figures 7-8; plate 4, figure 10; plate 5, figure 9	Grey shales of the Assilina granulosa Zone, Khuiala Formation (Lower Eocene), section III.	Carapace elongate-ovate in lateral view; maximum height at anterodorsal angle; left valve slightly overlapping right valve along dorsal and posterior margins. Carapace ear-shaped in lateral outline, with greatest height at anterior cardinal angle; left valve overlapping right valve along dorsal margin; dorsal margin nearly straight and sloping down backwardly; posterior cardinal angle distinct: ventral margin sinuate anteriorly but convex posteriorly; anterior margin broadly rounded; posterior margin drawn out in a caudal process in lower half and with 2-3 short spines: in dorsal view carapace spindle-shaped, with maximum width posterior to middle. Eye tubercle present at anterior cardinal angle. Inner lamella of moderate width; line of concrescence and inner margin coincide; selvage near outer margin; marginal pore canals straight as well as bifurcating, about 20-21 along anterior margin and about 5-6 along posterior margin. Hinge amphidont/heterodont; in right valve tt consists of an anterior tooth, followed by an anteromedian socket, a long posteromedian groove, and then a broad posterior tooth; in left valve hinge complementary and with a distinct accommodation groove.	Pokornyella bhatiai n. sp. resembles Pokornyella pindaraensis described by Khosla (1978) from the Lower Miocene beds of Saurashtra, Gujarat, in surface ornamentation but differs in having greatest height near anterior cardinal angle and straight dorsal margin. 910									Krithe		Krithe cf. K. solomoni	Honigstein, 1984	Krithe cf. K. solomoni Honigstein. - BASSIOUNI and LUGER 1990, p. 795, pl. 6, figs. 3, 6, 9, 12.	Plate 1, figures 8-9			Male specimens of Krithe cf. K. solomoni are lower and narrower than females. Our specimens are similar to those, reported from the Paleocene of Egypt (Bassiouni and Luger 1990), but the here figured specimens are characterized by a more straight and truncated posterior end. Krithe cf. solomoni is found commonly within the Mor (upper part), Horsha, Matred, Qeziot and Har Aqrav formations.			"0.69*0.33*0.40(F);

911									Krithe		Krithe benjaminii	Honigstein and Rosenfeld, 2002		Plate 1, figures 10-11	Har Qeren, sample BG 947, coord. 1025/ 0406 (Israeli Grid).	Large species of Krithe with elongated outline. In dorsal view subovate. Dorsal margin faintly convex, ventral margin almost straight. Anterior end evenly rounded, posterior end oblique, acutely truncated ventrally. Large, round depression situated in the center of the posterior face. Maximum height and width centrally. Valves nearly equal. Surface smooth. Distinct sexual dimorphism: Length/width ratio from 2.0 (in females) to nearly 3.0 (in males).	Large Krithe with oblique posterior end, towards the ventral margin acutely truncated posterior end. Large depression in the central part of the posterior end. Pronounced sexual dimorphism.	"Krithe benjaminii n. sp. is similar to K. echolsae Esker 1968 (p. 330, pl. 3, figs. 1-4; Paleocene of Tunisia), but differs mainly by its steeper truncation, located more posteriorly. Most of the figured specimens of K. echolsae are less elongate and smaller ( Bassiouni and Luger 1990, p. 795, pl. 6, figs. 10-11; Paleocene of Egypt; and Honigstein and Rosenfeld 1995, p. 53, pl. 1, figs. 4-5; Paleocene of Israel). Krithe bartonensis (Jones) 1857 ( Elewa and Ishizaki 1994, pl. 1, fig. 9; Middle Eocene of Egypt and Monostori 1996, pls. 11-12; Middle - Late Eocene of Hungary) resemblages in some features our new species, but is much smaller. Krithe benjaminii can be distinguished from K. cf. solomoni by its acute posterior end.
Krithe benjaminii is rare to common in samples from the Horsha, Matred and Nahal Yeter formations and common in the Qeziot and Har Aqrav formations."		"0.91*NA*0.42(F);
0.91*0.44*0.48(F);

919									Schizocythere		Schizocythere guerneti	Honigstein and Rosenfeld, 2002	"Schizocythere cf. S. tesselata (Bosquet). - KHALIFA and CRONIN 1979, p. 180, pl. 1, fig. 20.
Schizocythere sp., BOUKHARY et al. 1993, p. 196, pl. 5, fig. 10."	Plate 2, figures 6-7	"Type locality: Borot Ramalieh, coord. 1267/ 0221 (Israeli Grid), sample BG 851.
Type stratum: Horsha Formation"	Boukhary et al. (1993; Middle Eocene of Egypt) figured a species, called Schizocythere sp., and stated, after examination of the lectotype of Schizocythere tesselata (Bosquet) 1852, that, contrary to Khalifa and Cronin (1979; Middle Eocene of Egypt) it should not be referred to this species. Therefore, a new name is here designated. The described specimens are somewhat smaller than those of Khalifa and Cronin. The description of external features of Schizocythere guerneti n.sp. follows Khalifa and Cronin (1979, p. 180). Valves subequal; the left valve slightly overlapping the right one dorsally and ventrally. Sexual dimorphism not very pronounced: males are lower than females. Hinge schizodont. Left valve shows a crenulated anterior deep socket with five grooves, crenulated median bar, followed by a split tooth and a deeply subdivided socket posteriorly.	Small Schizocythere with regular longitudinal fossae as intercostate reticulation pattern, following the convex dorsal and ventral margins. Hinge typically schizodont.	Schizocythere guerneti occurs in rare-common quantities in the samples of the Mor (upper part), Horsha and Matred formations.		"0.39*NA*0.29(F);
0.39*0.24*0.25(M);

920									Paijenborchella		Paijenborchella druckmani	Honigstein and Rosenfeld, 2002		Plate 2, figures 8-9	"Type locality: Qeziot type section, coord. 0994/ 0280 (Israeli Grid); sample BG 917.
Type stratum: Qeziot Formation"	Small carapace, maximum height centrally. Dorsal margin straight to slightly sinusoidal subcentrally, ventral margin convex. Posterior margin with pronounced, long caudal process, truncated and situated centrally. Anterior margin rounded dorsally, ventrally built as angular fringe. Deep tranversal sulcus, originating at the dorsal margin and terminating at the ventral ridge. Anterior rim low and oblique, resulted by the compressed anterior area. Low gently convex dorsal rim, starting behind the sulcus and ending more rounded subcentrally in left valves. In right valves, this rim follows the dorsal margin till the posterior end. The dorsal ridge is almost connected with the pronounced ventral ridge, which follows the ventral margin. This ridge is ornamented with short perpendicular ribs. Relatively short, but prominent central ridge, bridging over the sulcus. Width greater than height; dorsal view subovoid with incision at the sulcus. Surface reticulated with irregular, coarse meshes, pitted in the peripheral areas. Interior features not observed (only carapaces found).	Small Paijenborchella with short median ridge, bridging the deep transversal sulcus. Dorsal rim low, gently convex. Ventral ridge prominent with short, perpendicular riblets. Intercostate coarse, irregular reticulation; peripheral zones pitted.	"Paijenborchella druckmani n. sp. is similar to P. trigona Marianos and Valentine (1958; Eocene of California; Carreno and Cronin 1993; Middle Eocene of Mexico), but differs from the latter mainly by its much shorter median ridge and a more elongated outline. Eopaijenborchella cf. lomata (Triebel) 1949 (see Bate and Robinson 1978, p. 416, pl. 9, fig. 13; Late Eocene of Britain) possesses approximately the same length of the median rib, but is much less reticulated.
P. druckmani is rare in samples of the Qeziot and Har Aqrav formations."		"0.52*0.30*0.26;
0.50*0.30*0.25;
0.46*0.30*0.25;"	Negev, Southern Israel	Ostracoda Zone:E-3. Type stratum: Qeziot Formation"	A new Mauritsina subspecies with well developed reticulation and spines. The intercostal elements from the dorsal to ventral margin are stronger than the longitudinal ones. A subdivided dorsal rib occurs at the ocular area. 935											Ordoniya tamorensis	Honigstein and Rosenfeld, 2002		Plate 4, figures 4-5		"Large to medium carapace subtriangular; greatest height at the anterior region. Anterior end broadly and equally rounded, posterior end pointed centrally. Exterior ends denticulate. Dorsal margin sinusoidal, ventral margin nearly straight. Ordoniya with circular rim, following the outer margins, and short, curved medium rib. Subcentral node and eye-spot weak.	Ordoniya tamorensis n. sp. was regarded by Honigstein and Rosenfeld (1995; Paleocene of Israel) as a new taxon, but only one carapace was found. It differs from 0. ordoniya (Bassiouni) 1971 (p. 31, pl. 4, figs. 4-8; Paleocene of Jordan) mainly by its much lower subcentral node and eye-spot. In addition, the circular rim in our species is finer.		"0.88*0.37*0.45;

937									Echinocythereis 		Echinocythereis aqravensis	Honigstein and Rosenfeld, 2002		Plate 4, figures 7-9		Medium sized carapaces, subrectangular; greatest height at the anterior cardinal angle. 943									Bradleya		Bradleya tongaensis	Hazel and Holden, 1971		"Plate 1, figures 10-12, 14-17, 20, 21; 
plate 3, figure 21"		In lateral view, carapace subquadrate, males more elongate, straight dorsal margin subparallel having slightly concave ventral margin, converging slightly toward posterior; anterior margin denticulate, obliquely rounded, somewhat flattened in dorsal half; posterior margin bluntly rounded, denticulate, having some larger denticles in ventral part; valves having two well-developed ridges, one extending from top of subcentral tubercle to posterodorsal angle along dorsum, the other from eye tubercle at anterodorsal angle, paralleling anterior margin, running along outer edge of large alalike swelling, terminating in prominent, outward pointing spine. Surface of valves covered by large fossae; six fossae bordering anterior margin, small ridges separating fossae with small elongated pits on upper surface. In dorsal view, carapace arrowhead shaped, greatest width in posterior quarter at alar spines; posterolateral surfaces compressed. Hinge amphidont; in right valve, anterior tooth smooth except in front where steplike; median elements consisting of postjacent socket and smooth groove; posterior tooth reniform, large, bilobate; lobation showing only on underside. Duplicature relatively narrow, no vestibules; well-developed selvage groove of right valve continuous, inner list well developed. Radial pore canals apparently simple, straight, abundant; many false canals extending through marginal denticles. Normal pores large, forming large pits on inner valve surface; pores tend to correspond with fossae of outer surface, but some extend through ridges between fossae. Muscle pit large, deep; four adductor-muscle scars positioned on posterior edge of pit, second scar from top largest and most elongated.	Distinguished by a straight alar ridge positioned low on the valve and resulting flat venter; reticulate subcentral tubercle well developed, grading posterodorsally with reticulate surface of valve.	This species is morphologically similar to Bradleya dictyon (Brady, 1880) and belongs to that Cenozoic species complex. It differs from B. dictyon (as illustrated by Hornibrook, 1952) in having a lower and straighter alar ridge, which results in a flat venter. In addition, there is no well-developed median ridge in B. tongaensis.		1.020*NA*0.581(LV)(F)	Eua, Tonga							Eocene	Late				Deep; Bathyal zone very near a tropical sublittoral environment. plate 3, figures 6, 7, 17, 18"		"Strongly alate; each valve having four prominent processes: (1) eye tubercle at antero-dorsal angle, (2) large hemispherical swelling, 200 JL wide, near dorsum just anterior to midlength, (3) posteroventral ala terminating in spine, (4) anterior swelling of alar ridge. All surfaces reticulate; left valve overlapping right valve above caudal process, anterodorsal angle, and ventral inturned area. Dimorphism not apparent. In lateral view, carapace wedge shaped; dorsal margin straight to posterodorsal area, profile broken by two dorsal swellings in anterior half; dorsal margin above caudal process slightly concave, ventrally inclined from horizontal dorsum; ventral margin broadly and evenly rounded to caudal process; anterior margin subtruncate, posterodorsal angle roughly 90°. In dorsal view, widest in posterior third at alae which project at almost right angles to valves, width equal to length; dorsolateral areas highly compressed, widening ventrally to greatest width at horizontal alar ridge running anterior to ala in ventral quarter.
Internally, large dorsolateral exterior tubercle and eye tubercle represented by deep sinuses; hinge of left valve having terminal sockets separated by long straight slightly crenulate bar that is thickened at ends; right valve complimentary."	Large bulbous swelling on anterodorso-lateral surface; prominent anterodorsal tubercle.	Bythocytheremorpha pacifica is somewhat similar to such Cretaceous species as B. bispinata (Weber, 1934), B. trituberculata (Herrig, 1963), and B. montuosa (Jones and Hinde, 1890), from which it is easily distinguished by the large dorso-lateral swelling. More similar is the living Pacific species B. tuberculata (Chapman, 1910) which possesses the dorsolateral swelling but which does not have the well-developed eye tubercle and is less acuminate at the posterior.		0.95*NA*0.438(LV)	Eua, Tonga							Eocene	Late				Deep; Bathyal zone very near a tropical sublittoral environment. 969			Latreilla	Podocopa		Cytheridae	Cytherinae		Schizocythere		Schizocythere gujeratensis	Guha, 1968		Pl. I, fig. 11-14, 16, 20		Shell small, rectangular oval with maximum height and thickness in the middle of the valve. Dorsal margin obscured by the dorsal ridges, ventral margin obscured by the ventral ridge. Anterior and broadly rounded, posterior end with a subdorsal rounded caudal process. Surface ornamentation consists of coarse reticulations and ridges. An anterior ridge starting from eyespot runs down and ends slightly above antero-ventral corner from where two longitudinal ridges run subparallel towards posterior end. Two ventral longitudinal ridges start from the anteroventral corner and end against a short prominent vertical ridge in the posteroventral part. Posterior to this, and slightly above, another vertical ridge is observed where the other two ridges merges. One dorsal ridge starting from eyespot runs upto posterior and where it thickens (seen in left valve only) and curves down and goes upto the caudal process. Another ridge runs below the dorsal ridge, merges with it in the middle, curves down and ends against a very prominent small thick vertical ridge slightly anterior to posterior cardinal angle. From the middle part of this vertical ridge two small ridges are noticed, one runs for a short distance towards caudal process, the other one towards middle part of the valve. The reticules are thick, rounded, tetragonal, the thick faces often merging together giving rise to number of small ridges.	The new species is very similar to Schizocythere appendlculata Triebel recorded from Lutetian of Paris basin, France (Triebel 1950) from which it differs in details of ornamentation.	Very common in the samples from Berwali and Lakhpat.		"0.45*0.29*0.30;

970									Cytheromorpha		Cytheromorpha kritharensis	Guha, 1968		Pl. I., fig. 5, 7 and 19.		Shell small, irregular oval, elongated, length being twice as much as its height, with maximum height and thickness at the anterior. Both ends are rounded, anterior being more evenly. Dorsal mergin straight sloping posteriorly. Ventral margin slightly concave in its middle. Surface ornamentation consist of small tetra-pentagonal reticulates with thin and low faces arranged more or less conscentrically around centre of the valve. A dorsal and ventral thin ridge starts from the anterior end and approach each other posteriorly and abruptly ends without merging, near the middle part of posterior end. The dorsal ridge is distinct posteriorly and in most specimens it is indistinct or absent.	The species resembles in shape and outline Cythermorpha calve Krutak (1961), recorded from Lower Jacson Eocene, Alabama from which it differs in being sculptured and smaller in size.	The species is common in Lakhpat and very rare in Berwali and Ghuar. Named after Kirthar beds of Kutch where first recorded.		"0.40*0.15*0.22;

975						Trachyleberididae			Acanthocythereis		Acanthocythereis bhujensis	Tewari and Tandon, 1960	Trachyleberis bhujensis (Tewari and Tandon), 1960				The forms described as Trachyleberis bhajensis probably belongs to the larval forms. In our collections, we recorded this species together with many adult specimens which show fine spines superimposed on weblike reticulations. The posterior hinge tooth of right valve is crenulated. The species fits very well with the genus Acanthocythereis rather than Trachyleberis. The spines are some time bifid or trifid specially the spines bordering the ends where they are aligned in a row parallel to them. The spines bordering the dorsal margin are less prominent compared to ventral margin and ends. The rest of the surface is having spines arranged in an irregular pattern except for 5-6 spines arranged in a longitudinal pattern slightly below and posterior to the eye spot. The spine on the dorsal margin near the posterior cardinal angle is most prominent. Both anterior and posterior ends are carrying prominent marginal spines. A weak subcentral tubercle is present.	Common in Lakhpat, Ghuar and Berwali.		0.60*0.22*0.32	Kutch, Gujerat state, western India		~43	~88				Eocene	Middle	Lutentian				limestone (major) and marl (minor)		Guha 1968 Ostracoda from Middle Eocene of Kutch, Gujerat State, western India.pdf
